# static-vs-dynamic-ip-in-router
I have a problem that when I connect my ESP 32 or phone to the router, how does the router know which IP my static device, and how does another device  and comunicte with static ip 

“I have an ESP32. I set a static IP, DNS, and subnet mask in my code. When the ESP32 connects to Wi-Fi, does it send the SSID, password, and the static IP configuration to the router during the connection process? And how does the router know which IP address to assign or allow in this case?”

Solution or explain

data-scroll-anchor="false"><h6 class="sr-only">ChatGPT said:</h6><div class="text-base my-auto mx-auto py-5 [--thread-content-margin:--spacing(4)] @[37rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(6)] @[70rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(12)] px-(--thread-content-margin)"><div class="[--thread-content-max-width:32rem] @[34rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:40rem] @[64rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:48rem] mx-auto flex max-w-(--thread-content-max-width) flex-1 text-base gap-4 md:gap-5 lg:gap-6 group/turn-messages focus-visible:outline-hidden" tabindex="-1"><div class="group/conversation-turn relative flex w-full min-w-0 flex-col agent-turn"><div class="relative flex-col gap-1 md:gap-3"><div class="flex max-w-full flex-col grow"><div data-message-author-role="assistant" data-message-id="3334fdf7-310e-46ea-9822-4c01799be695" dir="auto" class="min-h-8 text-message relative flex w-full flex-col items-end gap-2 text-start break-words whitespace-normal [.text-message+&amp;]:mt-5" data-message-model-slug="gpt-4o"><div class="flex w-full flex-col gap-1 empty:hidden first:pt-[3px]"><div class="markdown prose dark:prose-invert w-full break-words dark"><p data-start="0" data-end="110" class="">Great question, Ashish! Here's what happens when your ESP32 tries to connect to Wi-Fi using a static IP setup:</p>
<h3 data-start="112" data-end="178" class="">🔒 Does the ESP32 send SSID, password, and configuration data?</h3>
<p data-start="179" data-end="411" class="">Yes—but <strong data-start="187" data-end="240">only the SSID and password are sent to the router</strong>. The static IP configuration (IP, gateway, DNS, subnet) is not sent <strong data-start="309" data-end="315">to</strong> the router; instead, it’s <strong data-start="342" data-end="371">used locally by the ESP32</strong> to configure its own network interface.</p>
<p data-start="413" data-end="433" class="">Let’s break it down:</p>
<hr data-start="435" data-end="438" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="440" data-end="477" class="">✅ What ESP32 sends to the router:</h3>
<ul data-start="478" data-end="645">
<li data-start="478" data-end="548" class="" style="">
<p data-start="480" data-end="548" class=""><strong data-start="480" data-end="488">SSID</strong> (Wi-Fi name): Used to identify which network to connect to.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="549" data-end="645" class="" style="">
<p data-start="551" data-end="645" class=""><strong data-start="551" data-end="563">Password</strong>: Sent securely (WPA2 encryption if you're using it) during the handshake process.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="647" data-end="685" class="">This is standard for any Wi-Fi device.</p>
<hr data-start="687" data-end="690" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="692" data-end="733" class="">⚙️ What static IP config is used for:</h3>
<ul data-start="734" data-end="1024">
<li data-start="734" data-end="832" class="" style="">
<p data-start="736" data-end="832" class=""><strong data-start="736" data-end="749">Static IP</strong>: The IP address ESP32 will use instead of requesting one from the router via DHCP.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="833" data-end="917" class="" style="">
<p data-start="835" data-end="917" class=""><strong data-start="835" data-end="846">Gateway</strong>: The IP of your router, so ESP32 knows where to send outbound packets.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="918" data-end="969" class="" style="">
<p data-start="920" data-end="969" class=""><strong data-start="920" data-end="930">Subnet</strong>: Helps define the local network range.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="970" data-end="1024" class="" style="">
<p data-start="972" data-end="1024" class=""><strong data-start="972" data-end="979">DNS</strong>: ESP32 uses this for resolving domain names.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="1026" data-end="1127" class="">These settings are used <strong data-start="1050" data-end="1077">by the ESP32 internally</strong>—not broadcasted to or negotiated with the router.</p>
<hr data-start="1129" data-end="1132" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="1134" data-end="1159" class="">👇 Typical code flow:</h3>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="1160" data-end="1250"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div class="flex items-center text-token-text-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between h-9 bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary select-none rounded-t-[5px]">cpp</div><div class="sticky top-9"><div class="absolute end-0 bottom-0 flex h-9 items-center pe-2"><div class="bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary text-token-text-secondary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary flex items-center rounded-sm px-2 font-sans text-xs"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center select-none px-4 py-1" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path d="M2.5 5.5C4.3 5.2 5.2 4 5.5 2.5C5.8 4 6.7 5.2 8.5 5.5C6.7 5.8 5.8 7 5.5 8.5C5.2 7 4.3 5.8 2.5 5.5Z" fill="currentColor" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M5.66282 16.5231L5.18413 19.3952C5.12203 19.7678 5.09098 19.9541 5.14876 20.0888C5.19933 14.1657C6.24513 14.4392 6.09299 14.7348 5.97903 15.0458C5.85062 15.3963 5.78802 15.7719 5.66282 16.5231Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M14.5 7L18.5 11" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></svg>Edit</button></span></div></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="whitespace-pre! language-cpp"><span><span>WiFi.</span><span><span class="hljs-built_in">config</span></span><span>(local_IP, gateway, subnet, primaryDNS);
WiFi.</span><span><span class="hljs-built_in">begin</span></span><span>(ssid, password);
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="1252" data-end="1356" class="">Only <code data-start="1257" data-end="1285">WiFi.begin(ssid, password)</code> involves communication with the router (via encrypted WPA2 handshake).</p>
<hr data-start="1358" data-end="1361" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="1363" data-end="1384" class="">🔐 Security Note:</h3>
<ul data-start="1385" data-end="1517">
<li data-start="1385" data-end="1448" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1387" data-end="1448" class="">SSID and password are encrypted if your router uses WPA/WPA2.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1449" data-end="1517" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1451" data-end="1517" class="">The static config is never sent over the air, so no worries there.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="1519" data-end="1667" class="">Let me know if you want to see exactly how to debug or monitor this handshake using tools like Wireshark (useful for curiosity or security testing).</p></div></div></div></div><div class="flex absolute start-0 end-0 flex justify-start"><div class="touch:-me-2 touch:-ms-3.5 -ms-2.5 -me-1 flex items-center p-1 select-none -mt-1 data-scroll-anchor="false" style=""><h6 class="sr-only">ChatGPT said:</h6><div class="text-base my-auto mx-auto py-5 [--thread-content-margin:--spacing(4)] @[37rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(6)] @[70rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(12)] px-(--thread-content-margin)"><div class="[--thread-content-max-width:32rem] @[34rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:40rem] @[64rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:48rem] mx-auto flex max-w-(--thread-content-max-width) flex-1 text-base gap-4 md:gap-5 lg:gap-6 group/turn-messages focus-visible:outline-hidden" tabindex="-1"><div class="group/conversation-turn relative flex w-full min-w-0 flex-col agent-turn"><div class="relative flex-col gap-1 md:gap-3"><div class="flex max-w-full flex-col grow"><div data-message-author-role="assistant" data-message-id="1e57914d-0fa9-4cd4-a419-ea62f7d75371" dir="auto" class="min-h-8 text-message relative flex w-full flex-col items-end gap-2 text-start break-words whitespace-normal [.text-message+&amp;]:mt-5" data-message-model-slug="gpt-4o"><div class="flex w-full flex-col gap-1 empty:hidden first:pt-[3px]"><div class="markdown prose dark:prose-invert w-full break-words dark"><p data-start="0" data-end="132" class="">Ahh great follow-up, Ashish — this is a common point of confusion when working with static IPs on the ESP32 (or any network device).</p>
<p data-start="134" data-end="162" class="">Let’s break it down clearly:</p>
<hr data-start="164" data-end="167" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="169" data-end="218" class="">🧠 How your router knows what IP to "expect":</h3>
<p data-start="220" data-end="359" class="">When <strong data-start="225" data-end="261">you set a static IP on the ESP32</strong>, it <strong data-start="266" data-end="281">doesn't ask</strong> the router for one via DHCP. Instead, the ESP32 just <strong data-start="335" data-end="354">starts using it</strong>. So…</p>
<blockquote data-start="361" data-end="450">
<p data-start="363" data-end="450" class="">🚨 The router doesn’t “know” about it beforehand — it just sees a device using that IP.</p>
</blockquote>
<hr data-start="452" data-end="455" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="457" data-end="494" class="">✅ What happens behind the scenes:</h3>
<ol data-start="496" data-end="970">
<li data-start="496" data-end="625" class="" style="">
<p data-start="499" data-end="525" class=""><strong data-start="499" data-end="525">ESP32 sets its own IP:</strong></p>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="529" data-end="597"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div class="flex items-center text-token-text-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between h-9 bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary select-none rounded-t-[5px]">cpp</div><div class="sticky top-9"><div class="absolute end-0 bottom-0 flex h-9 items-center pe-2"><div class="bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary text-token-text-secondary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary flex items-center rounded-sm px-2 font-sans text-xs"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center select-none px-4 py-1" aria-label="Copy"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5C7 3.34315 8.34315 2 10 2H19C20.6569 2 22 3.34315 22 5V14C22 15.6569 20.6569 17 19 17H17V19C17 20.6569 15.6569 22 14 22H5C3.34315 22 2 20.6569 2 19V10C2 8.34315 3.34315 7 5 7H7V5ZM9 7H14C15.6569 7 17 8.34315 17 10V15H19C19.5523 15 20 14.5523 20 14V5C20 4.44772 19.5523 4 19 4H10C9.44772 4 9 4.44772 9 5V7ZM5 9C4.44772 9 4 9.44772 4 10V19C4 19.5523 4.44772 20 5 20H14C14.5523 20 15 19.5523 15 19V10C15 9.44772 14.5523 9 14 9H5Z" fill="currentColor"></path></svg>Copy</button></span><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex items-center gap-1 px-4 py-1 select-none"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path d="M2.5 5.5C4.3 5.2 5.2 4 5.5 2.5C5.8 4 6.7 5.2 8.5 5.5C6.7 5.8 5.8 7 5.5 8.5C5.2 7 4.3 5.8 2.5 5.5Z" fill="currentColor" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M5.66282 16.5231L5.18413 19.3952C5.12203 19.7678 5.09098 19.9541 5.14876 20.0888C5.19933 20.2067 5.29328 20.3007 5.41118 20.3512C5.54589 20.409 5.73218 20.378 6.10476 20.3159L8.97693 19.8372C9.72813 19.712 10.1037 19.6494 10.4542 19.521C10.7652 19.407 11.0608 19.2549 11.3343 19.068C11.6425 18.8575 11.9118 18.5882 12.4503 18.0497L20 10.5C21.3807 9.11929 21.3807 6.88071 20 5.5C18.6193 4.11929 16.3807 4.11929 15 5.5L7.45026 13.0497C6.91175 13.5882 6.6425 13.8575 6.43197 14.1657C6.24513 14.4392 6.09299 14.7348 5.97903 15.0458C5.85062 15.3963 5.78802 15.7719 5.66282 16.5231Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M14.5 7L18.5 11" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></svg>Edit</button></span></div></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="whitespace-pre! language-cpp"><span><span>WiFi.</span><span><span class="hljs-built_in">config</span></span><span>(local_IP, gateway, subnet, primaryDNS);
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="601" data-end="625" class="">Example: <code data-start="610" data-end="625">192.168.0.100</code></p>
</li>
<li data-start="627" data-end="724" class="" style="">
<p data-start="630" data-end="724" class=""><strong data-start="630" data-end="658">ESP32 sends ARP requests</strong> when it wants to talk on the network, just like any other device.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="726" data-end="970" class="" style="">
<p data-start="729" data-end="804" class=""><strong data-start="729" data-end="756">Router sees the traffic</strong> from <code data-start="762" data-end="777">192.168.0.100</code> and accepts it as long as:</p>
<ul data-start="808" data-end="970">
<li data-start="808" data-end="871" class="" style="">
<p data-start="810" data-end="871" class="">That IP isn’t already being used (by DHCP or another device),</p>
</li>
<li data-start="875" data-end="931" class="" style="">
<p data-start="877" data-end="931" class="">It’s within the router's subnet (e.g., <code data-start="916" data-end="929">192.168.0.x</code>),</p>
</li>
<li data-start="935" data-end="970" class="" style="">
<p data-start="937" data-end="970" class="">And the gateway is correctly set.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<hr data-start="972" data-end="975" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="977" data-end="1005" class="">🛑 But here's the catch:</h3>
<p data-start="1006" data-end="1153" class="">If your router’s <strong data-start="1023" data-end="1079">DHCP server might also try to assign <code data-start="1062" data-end="1077">192.168.0.100</code></strong> to some other device, there could be an <strong data-start="1120" data-end="1135">IP conflict</strong>. To prevent that:</p>
<hr data-start="1155" data-end="1158" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="1160" data-end="1205" class="">🛠️ Best Practices when using Static IPs:</h3>
<h4 data-start="1207" data-end="1262" class="">✅ Option 1: Reserve IP in the Router (Recommended)</h4>
<ul data-start="1263" data-end="1398">
<li data-start="1263" data-end="1292" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1265" data-end="1292" class="">Go to your router settings.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1293" data-end="1348" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1295" data-end="1348" class="">Reserve <code data-start="1303" data-end="1318">192.168.0.100</code> for your ESP32’s MAC address.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1349" data-end="1398" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1351" data-end="1398" class="">Now your router won’t assign it to anyone else.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h4 data-start="1400" data-end="1451" class="">✅ Option 2: Use IPs <strong data-start="1425" data-end="1451">outside the DHCP range</strong></h4>
<ul data-start="1452" data-end="1558">
<li data-start="1452" data-end="1558" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1454" data-end="1558" class="">If your router gives out IPs in range <code data-start="1492" data-end="1520">192.168.0.2 – 192.168.0.99</code>, use <code data-start="1526" data-end="1542">192.168.0.100+</code> for your ESP32.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="1560" data-end="1563" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="1565" data-end="1583" class="">🧪 Quick Test:</h3>
<ul data-start="1584" data-end="1757">
<li data-start="1584" data-end="1609" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1586" data-end="1609" class="">Set static IP in ESP32.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1610" data-end="1669" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1612" data-end="1669" class="">Connect and ping from your computer: <code data-start="1649" data-end="1669">ping 192.168.0.100</code></p>
</li>
<li data-start="1670" data-end="1757" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1672" data-end="1757" class="">Log into your router and check connected devices — ESP32 should show up with that IP.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="1759" data-end="1762" class="" style="">

data-scroll-anchor="false" style=""><h6 class="sr-only">ChatGPT said:</h6><div class="text-base my-auto mx-auto py-5 [--thread-content-margin:--spacing(4)] @[37rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(6)] @[70rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(12)] px-(--thread-content-margin)"><div class="[--thread-content-max-width:32rem] @[34rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:40rem] @[64rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:48rem] mx-auto flex max-w-(--thread-content-max-width) flex-1 text-base gap-4 md:gap-5 lg:gap-6 group/turn-messages <ul data-start="116" data-end="261">
<li data-start="116" data-end="136" class="" style="">
<p data-start="118" data-end="136" class="">🔹 What’s <strong data-start="128" data-end="136">DHCP</strong></p>
</li>
<li data-start="137" data-end="156" class="" style="">
<p data-start="139" data-end="156" class="">🔹 What’s <strong data-start="149" data-end="156">ARP</strong></p>
</li>
<li data-start="157" data-end="182" class="" style="">
<p data-start="159" data-end="182" class="">🔹 What’s <strong data-start="169" data-end="182">Handshake</strong></p>
</li>
<li data-start="183" data-end="261" class="" style="">
<p data-start="185" data-end="261" class="">🔹 And <strong data-start="192" data-end="231">how ESP32 connects with a static IP</strong> and how the router handles it</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="263" data-end="266" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="268" data-end="294" class="">🔌 1. What is <strong data-start="285" data-end="293">DHCP</strong>?</h2>
<p data-start="296" data-end="342" class=""><strong data-start="296" data-end="304">DHCP</strong> = Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol</p>
<p data-start="344" data-end="432" class="">It’s like the <strong data-start="358" data-end="393">router’s address-giving machine</strong>. Imagine your router is a post office:</p>
<ul data-start="433" data-end="697">
<li data-start="433" data-end="530" class="" style="">
<p data-start="435" data-end="530" class="">Every device (ESP32, laptop, phone) comes and says: “Hey! I’m new here. Give me an IP address.”</p>
</li>
<li data-start="531" data-end="610" class="" style="">
<p data-start="533" data-end="610" class="">The router (DHCP server) gives an IP like: <code data-start="576" data-end="589">192.168.0.5</code>, <code data-start="591" data-end="604">192.168.0.6</code>, etc.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="611" data-end="697" class="" style="">
<p data-start="613" data-end="697" class="">This way, devices don’t need to know or choose their IP — they get it automatically.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="699" data-end="776" class="">📦 Without DHCP, devices need to set their IP manually (i.e., <strong data-start="761" data-end="774">static IP</strong>).</p>
<hr data-start="778" data-end="781" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="783" data-end="814" class="">🧠 2. What is <strong data-start="800" data-end="813">Static IP</strong>?</h2>
<p data-start="816" data-end="854" class="">When you <strong data-start="825" data-end="837">manually</strong> tell a device:</p>
<blockquote data-start="855" data-end="899">
<p data-start="857" data-end="899" class="">"Use this exact IP, and don’t ask anyone."</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="901" data-end="933" class="">For example, in your ESP32 code:</p>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="934" data-end="1148"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div class="flex items-center text-token-text-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between h-9 bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary select-none rounded-t-[5px]">cpp</div><div class="sticky top-9"><div class="absolute end-0 bottom-0 flex h-9 items-center pe-2"><div class="bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary text-token-text-secondary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary flex items-center rounded-sm px-2 font-sans text-xs"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center select-none px-4 py-1" aria-label="Copy"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5C7 3.34315 8.34315 2 10 2H19C20.6569 2 22 3.34315 22 5V14C22 15.6569 20.6569 17 19 17H17V19C17 20.6569 15.6569 22 14 22H5C3.34315 22 2 20.6569 2 19V10C2 8.34315 3.34315 7 5 7H7V5ZM9 7H14C15.6569 7 17 8.34315 17 10V15H19C19.5523 15 20 14.5523 20 14V5C20 4.44772 19.5523 4 19 4H10C9.44772 4 9 4.44772 9 5V7ZM5 9C4.44772 9 4 9.44772 4 10V19C4 19.5523 4.44772 20 5 20H14C14.5523 20 15 19.5523 15 19V10C15 9.44772 14.5523 9 14 9H5Z" fill="currentColor"></path></svg>Copy</button></span><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex items-center gap-1 px-4 py-1 select-none"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path d="M2.5 5.5C4.3 5.2 5.2 4 5.5 2.5C5.8 4 6.7 5.2 8.5 5.5C6.7 5.8 5.8 7 5.5 8.5C5.2 7 4.3 5.8 2.5 5.5Z" fill="currentColor" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M5.66282 16.5231L5.18413 19.3952C5.12203 19.7678 5.09098 19.9541 5.14876 20.0888C5.19933 20.2067 5.29328 20.3007 5.41118 20.3512C5.54589 20.409 5.73218 20.378 6.10476 20.3159L8.97693 19.8372C9.72813 19.712 10.1037 19.6494 10.4542 19.521C10.7652 19.407 11.0608 19.2549 11.3343 19.068C11.6425 18.8575 11.9118 18.5882 12.4503 18.0497L20 10.5C21.3807 9.11929 21.3807 6.88071 20 5.5C18.6193 4.11929 16.3807 4.11929 15 5.5L7.45026 13.0497C6.91175 13.5882 6.6425 13.8575 6.43197 14.1657C6.24513 14.4392 6.09299 14.7348 5.97903 15.0458C5.85062 15.3963 5.78802 15.7719 5.66282 16.5231Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M14.5 7L18.5 11" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></svg>Edit</button></span></div></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="whitespace-pre! language-cpp"><span><span><span class="hljs-function">IPAddress <span class="hljs-title">local_IP</span></span></span><span><span class="hljs-params">(<span class="hljs-number">192</span></span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">168</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">0</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">100</span></span><span>);  </span><span><span class="hljs-comment">// Static IP</span></span><span>
</span><span><span class="hljs-function">IPAddress <span class="hljs-title">gateway</span></span></span><span><span class="hljs-params">(<span class="hljs-number">192</span></span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">168</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">0</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">1</span></span><span>);     </span><span><span class="hljs-comment">// Your router IP</span></span><span>
</span><span><span class="hljs-function">IPAddress <span class="hljs-title">subnet</span></span></span><span><span class="hljs-params">(<span class="hljs-number">255</span></span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">255</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">255</span></span><span>, </span><span><span class="hljs-number">0</span></span><span>);    </span><span><span class="hljs-comment">// Network mask</span></span><span>
WiFi.</span><span><span class="hljs-built_in">config</span></span><span>(local_IP, gateway, subnet);
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="1150" data-end="1171" class="">This tells the ESP32:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1172" data-end="1224">
<p data-start="1174" data-end="1224" class="">“Don’t talk to the DHCP server. Just use this IP.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="1226" data-end="1269" class="">Now, let’s see how the router handles this.</p>
<hr data-start="1271" data-end="1274" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="1276" data-end="1301" class="">🔎 3. What is <strong data-start="1293" data-end="1300">ARP</strong>?</h2>
<p data-start="1303" data-end="1340" class=""><strong data-start="1303" data-end="1310">ARP</strong> = Address Resolution Protocol</p>
<p data-start="1342" data-end="1359" class="">It’s like asking:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1360" data-end="1421">
<p data-start="1362" data-end="1421" class="">“Hey, who has IP <code data-start="1379" data-end="1394">192.168.0.100</code>? What’s your MAC address?”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="1423" data-end="1506" class="">🧠 The MAC address is a unique ID for your ESP32’s Wi-Fi chip (like a fingerprint).</p>
<p data-start="1508" data-end="1521" class="">Example flow:</p>
<ul data-start="1522" data-end="1696">
<li data-start="1522" data-end="1572" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1524" data-end="1572" class="">ESP32 joins Wi-Fi with static IP <code data-start="1557" data-end="1572">192.168.0.100</code></p>
</li>
<li data-start="1573" data-end="1626" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1575" data-end="1626" class="">Another device (say your PC) wants to talk to ESP32</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1627" data-end="1667" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1629" data-end="1667" class="">PC does ARP: “Who owns 192.168.0.100?”</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1668" data-end="1696" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1670" data-end="1696" class="">ESP32 replies with its MAC</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="1698" data-end="1748" class="">🎯 So ARP helps devices find <strong data-start="1727" data-end="1748">who owns which IP</strong></p>
<hr data-start="1750" data-end="1753" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="1755" data-end="1786" class="">🤝 4. What is <strong data-start="1772" data-end="1785">Handshake</strong>?</h2>
<p data-start="1788" data-end="1843" class="">Handshake = Process of <strong data-start="1811" data-end="1843">securely connecting to Wi-Fi</strong></p>
<p data-start="1845" data-end="1862" class="">When ESP32 calls:</p>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="1863" data-end="1901"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div class="flex items-center text-token-text-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between h-9 bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary select-none rounded-t-[5px]">cpp</div><div class="sticky top-9"><div class="absolute end-0 bottom-0 flex h-9 items-center pe-2"><div class="bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary text-token-text-secondary dark:bg-token-main-surface-secondary flex items-center rounded-sm px-2 font-sans text-xs"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center select-none px-4 py-1" aria-label="Copy"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5C7 3.34315 8.34315 2 10 2H19C20.6569 2 22 3.34315 22 5V14C22 15.6569 20.6569 17 19 17H17V19C17 20.6569 15.6569 22 14 22H5C3.34315 22 2 20.6569 2 19V10C2 8.34315 3.34315 7 5 7H7V5ZM9 7H14C15.6569 7 17 8.34315 17 10V15H19C19.5523 15 20 14.5523 20 14V5C20 4.44772 19.5523 4 19 4H10C9.44772 4 9 4.44772 9 5V7ZM5 9C4.44772 9 4 9.44772 4 10V19C4 19.5523 4.44772 20 5 20H14C14.5523 20 15 19.5523 15 19V10C15 9.44772 14.5523 9 14 9H5Z" fill="currentColor"></path></svg>Copy</button></span><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex items-center gap-1 px-4 py-1 select-none"><svg width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="icon-xs"><path d="M2.5 5.5C4.3 5.2 5.2 4 5.5 2.5C5.8 4 6.7 5.2 8.5 5.5C6.7 5.8 5.8 7 5.5 8.5C5.2 7 4.3 5.8 2.5 5.5Z" fill="currentColor" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M5.66282 16.5231L5.18413 19.3952C5.12203 19.7678 5.09098 19.9541 5.14876 20.0888C5.19933 14.1657C6.24513 14.4392 6.09299 14.7348 5.97903 15.0458C5.85062 15.3963 5.78802 15.7719 5.66282 16.5231Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M14.5 7L18.5 11" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></svg>Edit</button></span></div></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="whitespace-pre! language-cpp"><span><span>WiFi.</span><span><span class="hljs-built_in">begin</span></span><span>(ssid, password);
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="1902" data-end="1945" class="">It starts a <strong data-start="1914" data-end="1927">handshake</strong> with your router:</p>
<ul data-start="1947" data-end="2157">
<li data-start="1947" data-end="2004" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1949" data-end="2004" class="">“I want to join this Wi-Fi (SSID). Here’s my password.”</p>
</li>
<li data-start="2005" data-end="2051" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2007" data-end="2051" class="">Router says, “Let’s do WPA2 authentication.”</p>
</li>
<li data-start="2052" data-end="2106" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2054" data-end="2106" class="">They exchange keys securely (this is all encrypted).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="2107" data-end="2157" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2109" data-end="2157" class="">If password is correct → ✅ connection is allowed</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="2159" data-end="2213" class="">📡 This happens <strong data-start="2175" data-end="2212">whether you use DHCP or static IP</strong>.</p>
<hr data-start="2215" data-end="2218" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="2220" data-end="2263" class="">💡 How the ESP32 connects with static IP</h2>
<p data-start="2265" data-end="2295" class="">Let’s put it all together now:</p>
<h3 data-start="2297" data-end="2326" class="">STEP-BY-STEP EXPLANATION:</h3>
<div class="group pointer-events-none relative flex justify-center *:pointer-events-auto"><span class="pointer-events-none absolute start-full top-4 z-10 hidden h-full w-fit ps-2 md:block" data-state="closed"><button class="hover:bg-token-main-surface-secondary text-token-text-secondary pointer-events-auto rounded-lg px-1 py-1 opacity-0 transition-opacity duration-200 7H7V5ZM9 7H14C15.6569 7 17 8.34315 17 10V15H19C19.5523 15 20 14.5523 20 14V5C20 4.44772 19.5523 4 19 4H10C9.44772 4 9 4.44772 9 5V7ZM5 9C4.44772 9 4 9.44772 4 10V19C4 19.5523 4.44772 20 5 data-start="2328" data-end="2805"><thead data-start="2328" data-end="2365"><tr data-start="2328" data-end="2365"><th data-start="2328" data-end="2335">Step</th><th data-start="2335" class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2406" data-end="2410">1</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2410" data-end="2453">ESP32 sets its own IP to <code data-start="2437" data-end="2452">192.168.0.100</code></td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2453" data-end="2470">You, via code</td></tr><tr data-start="2471" data-end="2548"><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2471" data-end="2475">2</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)] min-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)/3)]" data-start="2475" data-end="2523">ESP32 connects to Wi-Fi using SSID + password</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2523" data-end="2548">Handshake with router</td></tr><tr data-start="2549" data-end="2619"><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2549" data-end="2553">3</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)] min-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)/3)]" data-start="2553" data-end="2599">ESP32 starts using <code data-start="2574" data-end="2589">192.168.0.100</code> directly</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2599" data-end="2619">No DHCP involved</td></tr><tr data-start="2620" data-end="2712"><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2620" data-end="2624">4</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)] min-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)/3)]" data-start="2624" data-end="2678">Router sees the device talking from <code data-start="2662" data-end="2677">192.168.0.100</code></td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2678" data-end="2712">Accepts it, if not in conflict</td></tr><tr data-start="2713" data-end="2805"><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2713" data-end="2717">5</td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)] min-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)/3)]" data-start="2717" data-end="2781">Other devices use ARP to find ESP32's MAC for <code data-start="2765" data-end="2780">192.168.0.100</code></td><td class="max-w-[calc(var(--thread-content-max-width)*2/3)]" data-start="2781" data-end="2805">Communication begins</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div>
<p data-start="2807" data-end="2855" class="">✅ If everything is correct — network works fine!</p>
<hr data-start="2857" data-end="2860" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="2862" data-end="2886" class="">⚠️ What can go wrong?</h2>
<p data-start="2888" data-end="2979" class="">If some <strong data-start="2896" data-end="2950">other device already got <code data-start="2923" data-end="2938">192.168.0.100</code> from DHCP</strong>, now there’s a <strong data-start="2966" data-end="2978">conflict</strong>.</p>
<p data-start="2981" data-end="2995" class="">That's why we:</p>
<ul data-start="2996" data-end="3095">
<li data-start="2996" data-end="3062" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2998" data-end="3062" class="">Reserve the IP in router for ESP32’s MAC (optional but safe), OR</p>
</li>
<li data-start="3063" data-end="3095" class="" style="">
<p data-start="3065" data-end="3095" class="">Pick IPs outside of DHCP range</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="3097" data-end="3100" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="3102" data-end="3115" class="">🧪 Summary</h2>

data-scroll-anchor="false" style=""><h6 class="sr-only">ChatGPT said:</h6><div class="text-base my-auto mx-auto py-5 [--thread-content-margin:--spacing(4)] @[37rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(6)] @[70rem]:[--thread-content-margin:--spacing(12)] px-(--thread-content-margin)"><div class="[--thread-content-max-width:32rem] @[34rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:40rem] @[64rem]:[--thread-content-max-width:48rem] mx-auto flex max-w-(--thread-content-max-width) flex-1 text-base gap-4 md:gap-5 lg:gap-6 group/turn-messages focus-visible:outline-hidden" tabindex="-1"><div class="group/conversation-turn relative flex w-full min-w-0 flex-col agent-turn"><div class="relative flex-col gap-1 md:gap-3"><div class="flex max-w-full flex-col grow"><div data-message-author-role="assistant" data-message-id="858e9e8f-7fb2-4108-a3ec-425f2e0d124a" dir="auto" class="min-h-8 text-message relative flex w-full flex-col items-end gap-2 text-start break-words whitespace-normal [.text-message+&amp;]:mt-5" data-message-model-slug="gpt-4o"><div class="flex w-full flex-col gap-1 empty:hidden first:pt-[3px]"><div class="markdown prose dark:prose-invert w-full break-words dark"><p data-start="0" data-end="142" class="">Exactly, Ashish! That’s a <strong data-start="26" data-end="45">perfect analogy</strong> — let's build on your <strong data-start="68" data-end="85">hotel &amp; rooms</strong> example to understand everything even more clearly. 🏨💡</p>
<hr data-start="144" data-end="147" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="149" data-end="171" class="">🏨 Router = Hotel</h2>
<h2 data-start="172" data-end="200" class="">🚪 IP Addresses = Rooms</h2>
<h2 data-start="201" data-end="252" class="">🧍 Devices = Guests (ESP32, phone, laptop, etc.)</h2>
<hr data-start="254" data-end="257" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="259" data-end="301" class="">✅ CASE 1: <strong data-start="273" data-end="301">Using DHCP (default way)</strong></h3>
<p data-start="303" data-end="360" class=""><strong data-start="303" data-end="312">Guest</strong> arrives at the hotel lobby (router).<br data-start="349" data-end="352">
He says:</p>
<blockquote data-start="362" data-end="422">
<p data-start="364" data-end="422" class="">“Hi! I want to stay here, but I don’t have a room number.”</p>
</blockquote>
<h3 data-start="424" data-end="462" class="">🧑‍✈️ Hotel Reception (DHCP) says:</h3>
<blockquote data-start="463" data-end="521">
<p data-start="465" data-end="521" class="">“No problem! I’ll assign you a free room automatically.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="523" data-end="548" class="">👉 So the router gives:</p>
<blockquote data-start="549" data-end="603">
<p data-start="551" data-end="603" class="">“You get Room 192.168.0.5 — use it until you leave.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="605" data-end="692" class="">📌 Every new device gets a free room, dynamically (temporary). This is called <strong data-start="683" data-end="691">DHCP</strong>.</p>
<hr data-start="694" data-end="697" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="699" data-end="732" class="">✅ CASE 2: <strong data-start="713" data-end="732">Using Static IP</strong></h3>
<p data-start="734" data-end="788" class="">Now let’s say another guest (ESP32) walks in and says:</p>
<blockquote data-start="790" data-end="876">
<p data-start="792" data-end="876" class="">“Hey, I don’t need a room assigned. I already picked Room 192.168.0.100 for myself.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="878" data-end="929" class="">If that room is <strong data-start="894" data-end="903">empty</strong>, the hotel (router) says:</p>
<blockquote data-start="930" data-end="997">
<p data-start="932" data-end="997" class="">“Okay fine. You’re already inside the building. Enjoy your stay.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="999" data-end="1003" class="">But…</p>
<p data-start="1005" data-end="1067" class="">If <strong data-start="1008" data-end="1060">someone else already occupies Room 192.168.0.100</strong>, then:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1068" data-end="1106">
<p data-start="1070" data-end="1106" class="">❌ There's a fight! ⚠️ Room conflict!</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="1108" data-end="1193" class="">That’s why it’s important to pick a room (IP) <strong data-start="1154" data-end="1192">not used by DHCP or another device</strong>.</p>
<hr data-start="1195" data-end="1198" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="1200" data-end="1239" class="">🔐 Wi-Fi Password = Hotel Entry Code</h2>
<p data-start="1241" data-end="1283" class="">Before you can get <strong data-start="1260" data-end="1272">any room</strong>, you must:</p>
<ul data-start="1284" data-end="1453">
<li data-start="1284" data-end="1343" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1286" data-end="1343" class="">Show the correct <strong data-start="1303" data-end="1315">password</strong> to enter the hotel (Wi-Fi).</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1344" data-end="1378" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1346" data-end="1378" class="">This is the <strong data-start="1358" data-end="1377">Wi-Fi handshake</strong>.</p>
</li>
<li data-start="1379" data-end="1453" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1381" data-end="1453" class="">If your password is wrong, the router (hotel security) won’t let you in.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<hr data-start="1455" data-end="1458" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="1460" data-end="1487" class="">🔁 ARP = Room Directory</h3>
<p data-start="1489" data-end="1518" class="">Once you’re inside the hotel:</p>
<ul data-start="1519" data-end="1689">
<li data-start="1519" data-end="1590" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1521" data-end="1546" class="">Other guests might say:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1549" data-end="1590">
<p data-start="1551" data-end="1590" class="">“Who is staying in Room 192.168.0.100?”</p>
</blockquote>
</li>
<li data-start="1592" data-end="1635" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1594" data-end="1609" class="">The hotel asks:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1612" data-end="1635">
<p data-start="1614" data-end="1635" class="">“Who owns this room?”</p>
</blockquote>
</li>
<li data-start="1637" data-end="1689" class="" style="">
<p data-start="1639" data-end="1658" class="">Your ESP32 replies:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1661" data-end="1689">
<p data-start="1663" data-end="1689" class="">“That’s me!” (this is ARP)</p>
</blockquote>
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="1691" data-end="1747" class="">So now everyone knows where you are and can talk to you.</p>
<hr data-start="1749" data-end="1752" class="" style="">
<h2 data-start="1754" data-end="1769" class="">📝 In short:</h2>

ChatGPT said:
Gotcha, Ashish! Let's break it down super simple, step-by-step. By the end of this, you'll clearly understand:

🔹 What’s DHCP

🔹 What’s ARP

🔹 What’s Handshake

🔹 And how ESP32 connects with a static IP and how the router handles it

🔌 1. What is DHCP?
DHCP = Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol

It’s like the router’s address-giving machine. Imagine your router is a post office:

Every device (ESP32, laptop, phone) comes and says: “Hey! I’m new here. Give me an IP address.”

The router (DHCP server) gives an IP like: 192.168.0.5, 192.168.0.6, etc.

This way, devices don’t need to know or choose their IP — they get it automatically.

📦 Without DHCP, devices need to set their IP manually (i.e., static IP).

🧠 2. What is Static IP?
When you manually tell a device:

"Use this exact IP, and don’t ask anyone."

For example, in your ESP32 code:

cpp
Copy
Edit
IPAddress local_IP(192, 168, 0, 100);  // Static IP
IPAddress gateway(192, 168, 0, 1);     // Your router IP
IPAddress subnet(255, 255, 255, 0);    // Network mask
WiFi.config(local_IP, gateway, subnet);
This tells the ESP32:

“Don’t talk to the DHCP server. Just use this IP.”

Now, let’s see how the router handles this.

🔎 3. What is ARP?
ARP = Address Resolution Protocol

It’s like asking:

“Hey, who has IP 192.168.0.100? What’s your MAC address?”

🧠 The MAC address is a unique ID for your ESP32’s Wi-Fi chip (like a fingerprint).

Example flow:

ESP32 joins Wi-Fi with static IP 192.168.0.100

Another device (say your PC) wants to talk to ESP32

PC does ARP: “Who owns 192.168.0.100?”

ESP32 replies with its MAC

🎯 So ARP helps devices find who owns which IP

🤝 4. What is Handshake?
Handshake = Process of securely connecting to Wi-Fi

When ESP32 calls:

cpp
Copy
Edit
WiFi.begin(ssid, password);
It starts a handshake with your router:

“I want to join this Wi-Fi (SSID). Here’s my password.”

Router says, “Let’s do WPA2 authentication.”

They exchange keys securely (this is all encrypted).

If password is correct → ✅ connection is allowed

📡 This happens whether you use DHCP or static IP.

💡 How the ESP32 connects with static IP
Let’s put it all together now:

STEP-BY-STEP EXPLANATION:

Step	What Happens	Who Does It
1	ESP32 sets its own IP to 192.168.0.100	You, via code
2	ESP32 connects to Wi-Fi using SSID + password	Handshake with router
3	ESP32 starts using 192.168.0.100 directly	No DHCP involved
4	Router sees the device talking from 192.168.0.100	Accepts it, if not in conflict
5	Other devices use ARP to find ESP32's MAC for 192.168.0.100	Communication begins
✅ If everything is correct — network works fine!

⚠️ What can go wrong?
If some other device already got 192.168.0.100 from DHCP, now there’s a conflict.

That's why we:

Reserve the IP in router for ESP32’s MAC (optional but safe), OR

Pick IPs outside of DHCP range

🧪 Summary

Term	Meaning
DHCP	Router auto-gives IP addresses
Static IP	You manually set the IP
ARP	Devices ask “who owns this IP?”
Handshake	Secure Wi-Fi connection setup (uses SSID + password)
Let me know if you want me to draw a simple diagram for this process too — or walk you through setting a reserved IP in your Airtel ZTE router!







You said:
so u say that in a router is like a hotel and a rooms are like ip address. when a person come to hotel he just need security code to come to hotel and if he need static mean he can go to any room if no specifiation is given then dhcp is giving rooms dynamicly 


ChatGPT said:
Exactly, Ashish! That’s a perfect analogy — let's build on your hotel &amp; rooms example to understand everything even more clearly. 🏨💡

🏨 Router = Hotel
🚪 IP Addresses = Rooms
🧍 Devices = Guests (ESP32, phone, laptop, etc.)
✅ CASE 1: Using DHCP (default way)
Guest arrives at the hotel lobby (router).
He says:

“Hi! I want to stay here, but I don’t have a room number.”

🧑‍✈️ Hotel Reception (DHCP) says:
“No problem! I’ll assign you a free room automatically.”

👉 So the router gives:

“You get Room 192.168.0.5 — use it until you leave.”

📌 Every new device gets a free room, dynamically (temporary). This is called DHCP.

✅ CASE 2: Using Static IP
Now let’s say another guest (ESP32) walks in and says:

“Hey, I don’t need a room assigned. I already picked Room 192.168.0.100 for myself.”

If that room is empty, the hotel (router) says:

“Okay fine. You’re already inside the building. Enjoy your stay.”

But…

If someone else already occupies Room 192.168.0.100, then:

❌ There's a fight! ⚠️ Room conflict!

That’s why it’s important to pick a room (IP) not used by DHCP or another device.

🔐 Wi-Fi Password = Hotel Entry Code
Before you can get any room, you must:

Show the correct password to enter the hotel (Wi-Fi).

This is the Wi-Fi handshake.

If your password is wrong, the router (hotel security) won’t let you in.

🔁 ARP = Room Directory
Once you’re inside the hotel:

Other guests might say:

“Who is staying in Room 192.168.0.100?”

The hotel asks:

“Who owns this room?”

Your ESP32 replies:

“That’s me!” (this is ARP)

So now everyone knows where you are and can talk to you.

📝 In short:

Thing	Analogy	Real Meaning
Router	Hotel	The main network hub
IP address	Room number	Your identity in the network
DHCP	Reception assigns rooms	Router gives dynamic IPs
Static IP	Guest picks room himself	Manual IP assigned in code
Handshake	Show password at entry	Wi-Fi connection process
ARP	Asking who’s in a room	Find the device with that IP
MAC Address	ID card	Unique hardware ID
Do you want a simple cartoon-style diagram for this? I can make that visual too if it helps 📊✨

fill="currentColor" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M5.66282 16.5231L5.18413 19.3952C5.12203 19.7678 5.09098 19.9541 5.14876 20.0888C5.19933 20.2067 5.29328 20.3007 5.41118 20.3512C5.54589 20.409 5.73218 20.378 6.10476 20.3159L8.97693 19.8372C9.72813 19.712 10.1037 19.6494 10.4542 19.521C10.7652 19.407 11.0608 19.2549 11.3343 19.068C11.6425 18.8575 11.9118 18.5882 12.4503 18.0497L20 10.5C21.3807 9.11929 21.3807 6.88071 20 5.5C18.6193 4.11929 16.3807 4.11929 15 5.5L7.45026 13.0497C6.91175 13.5882 6.6425 13.8575 6.43197 14.1657C6.24513 14.4392 6.09299 14.7348 5.97903 15.0458C5.85062 15.3963 5.78802 15.7719 5.66282 16.5231Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path><path d="M14.5 7L18.5 11" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></svg>Edit</button></span></div></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="whitespace-pre! language-markdown"><span><span><span class="hljs-section">## 🧠 Networking Explained Like a Hotel – ESP32 Edition</span></span><span>

| 🔧 Concept     | 🏨 Analogy                 | 📘 Real Meaning                            |
|---------------|---------------------------|--------------------------------------------|
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**Router**</span></span><span>    | Hotel                     | The network hub (manages all traffic)      |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**IP Address**</span></span><span>| Room number               | Identity of each device in the network     |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**DHCP**</span></span><span>      | Reception gives rooms     | Router gives IP addresses dynamically      |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**Static IP**</span></span><span> | Guest picks own room      | Manually assigned IP by the device         |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**Handshake**</span></span><span> | Show password to enter    | Wi-Fi login/authentication                 |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**ARP**</span></span><span>       | Ask who owns a room       | Find MAC address of device with that IP    |
| </span><span><span class="hljs-strong">**MAC Address**</span></span><span> | ID card                 | Unique ID of device’s network interface    |

---

</span><span><span class="hljs-section">### 🧰 DHCP vs Static IP Example</span></span><span>

</span><span><span class="hljs-section">#### ✅ Case 1: DHCP</span></span><span>
Guest arrives and says:  
</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; “I don’t have a room, give me one.”</span></span><span>

Reception says:  
</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; “Here’s Room 192.168.0.5.”</span></span><span>

</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; ✔️ Automatically assigned by <span class="hljs-strong">**DHCP**</span></span></span><span>

</span><span><span class="hljs-section">#### ✅ Case 2: Static IP</span></span><span>
Guest says:  
</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; “I’m taking Room 192.168.0.100 myself.”</span></span><span>

If the room is empty:
</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; ✔️ Allowed — router accepts it.</span></span><span>

If the room is already taken:
</span><span><span class="hljs-quote">&gt; ❌ Conflict! Two devices, one IP.</span></span><span>

---

</span><span><span class="hljs-section">### 🔐 What is Handshake?</span></span><span>

When ESP32 runs:
<span class="hljs-code">```cpp
WiFi.begin(ssid, password);
</span></span></span></code></div></div></pre>
<p data-start="1926" data-end="1946" class="">It tells the router:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1947" data-end="1988">
<p data-start="1949" data-end="1988" class="">“Let me in! Here's the Wi-Fi password.”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="1990" data-end="1997" class="">Router:</p>
<blockquote data-start="1998" data-end="2037">
<p data-start="2000" data-end="2037" class="">“Okay, password matches — you're in!”</p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote data-start="2039" data-end="2089">
<p data-start="2041" data-end="2089" class="">This is called a <strong data-start="2058" data-end="2071">handshake</strong> (authentication).</p>
</blockquote>
<hr data-start="2091" data-end="2094" class="" style="">
<h3 data-start="2096" data-end="2115" class="">🔁 What is ARP?</h3>
<p data-start="2117" data-end="2150" class="">Once inside, another device asks:</p>
<blockquote data-start="2151" data-end="2184">
<p data-start="2153" data-end="2184" class="">“Who is in Room 192.168.0.100?”</p>
</blockquote>
<p data-start="2186" data-end="2210" class="">Router checks ARP table:</p>
<blockquote data-start="2211" data-end="2251">
<p data-start="2213" data-end="2251" class="">“ESP32 owns that room (based on MAC).”</p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote data-start="2253" data-end="2293">
<p data-start="2255" data-end="2293" class="">ARP helps devices <strong data-start="2273" data-end="2292">find each other</strong>.</p>
</blockquote>
<hr data-start="2295" data-end="2298" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2300" data-end="2349" class="">📌 <strong data-start="2303" data-end="2311">Tip:</strong> If using a static IP, make sure it’s:</p>
<ul data-start="2350" data-end="2414">
<li data-start="2350" data-end="2383" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2352" data-end="2383" class="">Outside the router’s DHCP range</p>
</li>
<li data-start="2384" data-end="2414" class="" style="">
<p data-start="2386" data-end="2414" class="">Not used by any other device</p>
</li>
</ul>
<pre class="overflow-visible!" data-start="2415" data-end="5431"><div class="contain-inline-size rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium relative bg-token-sidebar-surface-primary"><div       </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">td</span></span></span><span>&gt;ID card</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">td</span></span></span><span>&gt;
      </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">td</span></span></span><span>&gt;Unique ID of device’s network interface</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">td</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">tr</span></span></span><span>&gt;
  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">table</span></span></span><span>&gt;

  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"block"</span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"emoji"</span></span><span>&gt;✅ Case 1: DHCP</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;Guest: “I don’t have a room, give me one.”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">br</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    Reception: “Here’s Room </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;192.168.0.5</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;.”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">strong</span></span></span><span>&gt;✔️ Automatically assigned by DHCP</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">strong</span></span></span><span>&gt;</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span>&gt;

  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"block"</span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"emoji"</span></span><span>&gt;✅ Case 2: Static IP</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;Guest: “I’m taking Room </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;192.168.0.100</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt; myself.”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;If empty: ✔️ Allowed</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">br</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    If taken: ❌ Conflict!</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span>&gt;

  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"block"</span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"emoji"</span></span><span>&gt;🔐 What is Handshake?</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;ESP32 runs: </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;WiFi.begin(ssid, password);</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">br</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    It tells the router: “Here’s my password.”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">br</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    Router says: “Okay, you’re in!”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span>&gt;

  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"block"</span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span> </span><span><span class="hljs-attr">class</span></span><span>=</span><span><span class="hljs-string">"emoji"</span></span><span>&gt;🔁 What is ARP?</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">h3</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;PC asks: “Who’s in Room </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;192.168.0.100</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">code</span></span></span><span>&gt;?”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">br</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    Router checks and replies: “ESP32 owns it (MAC address).”</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
    </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">strong</span></span></span><span>&gt;✔️ ARP helps devices find each other</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">strong</span></span></span><span>&gt;</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">p</span></span></span><span>&gt;
  </span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">div</span></span></span><span>&gt;
</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">body</span></span></span><span>&gt;
</span><span><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;/<span class="hljs-name">html</span></span></span><span>&gt;
</span></span></code></div></div></pre>
